## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: The variables indicate a constitutive relation where stress (sigma) depends on strain (epsilon) and temperature (T), typical of thermoelasticity, plasticity with thermal softening, and high-temperature/creep material models used in materials science and mechanical engineering.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Isothermal linear elasticity (Hooke-type): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (elastic stiffness varying approximately linearly with T)
- Thermoelastic stress with thermal strain offset: sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * T) (stress from mechanical strain minus thermal expansion strain; T as temperature rise relative to a reference absorbed into constants)
- Quadratic/nonlinear elasticity: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + c2 * epsilon**2 (moderate nonlinearity in elastic response plus temperature-dependent stiffness)
- Exponential thermal softening of modulus: sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon (captures rapid stiffness loss with increasing T; c1 often negative in fits)
- Power-law strain hardening with thermal prefactor (Hollomon-type): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) * epsilon**c2 (plastic flow stress with strain hardening and temperature softening)
- Ludwik-type (offset yield + hardening): sigma = c0 * exp(c1 * T) + c2 * exp(c3 * T) * epsilon**c4 (yield/athermal component plus strain hardening, both temperature affected)
- Ramberg–Osgood inverted form (implicit-style explicit surrogate): sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(c3 * T) (captures elastic + nonlinear/plastic strain contribution with thermal softening)
- Johnson–Cook-like (strain hardening × thermal softening, simplified without strain-rate): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T)**c5 (multiplicative coupling between hardening and homologous-temperature-like softening proxy)
- Thermally activated flow (Eyring-type stress): sigma = c0 + c1 * asinh(c2 * epsilon) * T (often used as a surrogate for activation-controlled plasticity where stress scales with T times an inverse-sinh of strain-like driving)
- Entropic/hyperelastic rubber-like surrogate with temperature scaling: sigma = c0 * T * (epsilon - c1 / (epsilon + c2)) (captures temperature-proportional entropic stress with finite-extensibility-like stiffening)
- Piecewise elastic–plastic surrogate using smooth transition: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon + (c2 + c3 * T) * log(c4 * epsilon + 1) (elastic at small strain, then logarithmic hardening; temperature shifts both parts)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Thermal softening of stiffness/yield: factors like exp(c*T) or (c0 + c1*T) multiplying stiffness/hardening terms often represent modulus and flow-stress decreasing with T (negative slope/exponent).
- Thermal expansion-induced stress shift: forms like (epsilon - c*T) create an apparent strain offset; at fixed epsilon, sigma can drop roughly linearly with T due to increasing free thermal strain.
- Elastic-to-plastic transition: adding a second, slower-growing term (e.g., log(c*epsilon+1) or epsilon**n with n<1) to a linear elastic term mimics yielding/strain hardening onset without an explicit piecewise model.
- Strain hardening identification: sigma increasing faster than linear at larger epsilon suggests polynomial/higher-power terms; increasing slower than linear suggests log(1+c*epsilon) or epsilon**n with 0<n<1.
- Temperature-dependent hardening exponent: allowing the power n to vary with T (e.g., epsilon**(c0+c1*T)) can capture observed changes in work-hardening rate at elevated temperature.
- Coupled multiplicative structure: (hardening term in epsilon) * (softening term in T) is common when the same physical mechanism scales the entire flow curve with temperature.
- High-T creep-like signatures (in strain-only data): strong sensitivity to T with relatively weak dependence on epsilon can push models toward sigma ≈ g(T) + h(T)*f(epsilon), where g(T) dominates at high T.
- Finite extensibility / stiffening near large strain: rational terms like epsilon - c/(epsilon+c2) or rapidly increasing nonlinear terms can mimic steep upturns as microstructural limits are approached.

GT (fixed) is a sum of three qualitatively specific parts (in variables `epsilon, T`):

1) **Bilinear/affine in T, linear in epsilon**  
\[
3.6246\,\epsilon\Big(-0.0589918\,(T-367.023)+1\Big)
= \epsilon\,(A + B\,T)
\]
So the GT contains an \(\epsilon T\) term **and** an \(\epsilon\) term (no standalone \(T\) term).

2) **Arrhenius-type term with fractional power of epsilon**  
\[
94.2050\,\epsilon^{0.44749}\exp\!\Big(-\frac{55.0161}{8.314\,T}\Big)
\]
This is **exp(constant / T)** (specifically negative constant over \(T\)), multiplied by \(\epsilon^{0.44749}\).

3) **Gaussian in T multiplied by epsilon**  
\[
5.12428\,\epsilon\,\exp\!\big(-(T-367.023)^2\big)
\]
This is **exp( - (T-shift)^2 )** times \(\epsilon\).

To match GT (even on a plausible restricted domain), a candidate must be able to reproduce:
- an \(\epsilon\exp(\text{quadratic in }T)\) Gaussian factor (or something identical under a domain restriction),
- an \(\epsilon^{0.44749}\exp(\text{const}/T)\) Arrhenius factor,
- plus the linear-in-\(T\) times \(\epsilon\) piece.

I need to analyze the Ground Truth (GT) expression and compare each candidate to it.

**GT expression:**
```
3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*(T - 367.02) + 1) + 94.205*epsilon^0.4475*exp(-55.016/(8.314*T)) + epsilon*5.1243*exp(-(T - 367.02)^2)
```

Let me expand the first term:
```
3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 0.05899*367.02 + 1) = 3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 21.65 + 1) = 3.6246*epsilon*(-0.05899*T + 22.65)
```

So GT = A*T*epsilon + B*epsilon + C*epsilon^0.4475*exp(D/T) + E*epsilon*exp(-(T-F)^2)

where A = 3.6246*(-0.05899) ≈ -0.2139, B = 3.6246*22.65 ≈ 82.10, C = 94.205, D = -55.016/8.314 ≈ -6.617, E = 5.1243, F = 367.02.

The GT has these structural components:
1. **T*epsilon** (linear in both)
2. **epsilon** (linear)
3. **epsilon^0.4475 * exp(negative/T)** — a fractional power of epsilon times Arrhenius-type T dependence
4. **epsilon * exp(-(T-367)^2)** — epsilon times Gaussian in T

This is a complex expression with specific basis functions. Let me check each candidate.

**Key basis functions needed:**
- T*epsilon
- epsilon
- epsilon^(~0.45) * exp(const/T)
- epsilon * exp(-(T-const)^2) — Gaussian in T
